  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_33f7ad20-2a12-4bdc-b018-d7f77890d9d7'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText1108235491718768039" style="display:none"><b>One war. Too many deadly battles. Can a king save his kingdom when his own survival seems unlikely?</b><br /><br />War has come to Carthya. It knocks at every door and window in the land. And when Jaron learns that King Vargan of Avenia has kidnapped Imogen in a plot to bring Carthya to its knees, Jaron knows it is up to him to embark on a daring rescue mission. But everything that can go wrong does.<br /><br />His friends are flung far and wide across Carthya and its neighbouring lands. In a last-ditch effort to stave off what looks to be a devastating loss for the kingdom, Jaron undertakes what may be his last journey to save everything and everyone he loves. But even with his lightning-quick wit, Jaron cannot forestall the terrible danger that descends on him and his country. Along the way, will he lose what matters most? And in the end, who will sit on Carthya's throne?</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer865373400" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer672708834071757868">The first book in this trilogy is better as a stand-alone than with the other two. The second was good enough. This... I felt like I wasted my day reading it.<br/><br/>There were so many obvious twists, it was sort of pathetic. The main character felt sort of bland at this point. It also seemed like it was trying to be an actiony-adventure war story, but at the same time trying to apologize for making war look interesting, with what felt like throwaway lines about how horrific it all was. All in all, it j</span>
  <span id="freeText672708834071757868" style="display:none">The first book in this trilogy is better as a stand-alone than with the other two. The second was good enough. This... I felt like I wasted my day reading it.<br /><br />There were so many obvious twists, it was sort of pathetic. The main character felt sort of bland at this point. It also seemed like it was trying to be an actiony-adventure war story, but at the same time trying to apologize for making war look interesting, with what felt like throwaway lines about how horrific it all was. All in all, it just felt generic, like it was just going over well-trodden territory. I expected a lot more after the wonderful first book. <br />It also seemed ironic to me that the author mentioned in the acknowledgements a quote from Toni Morrison saying that if the book you want hasn't been written yet, write it yourself. I can think of so many books, comics, movies, etc. that have done a similar story, but better. It's been written. <br /><br />That said, the first one is definitely worth reading. Just not this one. </span>
  <a data-text-id="672708834071757868" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText17074887056489959986" style="display:none">My heart is aching while I'm writing my review on the final sequel of this series because it's hard to say goodbye to the books/novels you've been deeply attached with,especially with the best characters you'll surely miss..<br /><br />In here,Sage's character had grown strong because of his anger to what had happen to his country,that he plunges himself into a dangerous,reckless(as usual)attempt to save his country,his friends and the people he loves as he face the <b>WAR</b> from three different countries/kingdoms.And though I've been used to him,getting away with everything and out-witting even the most clever adult,I couldn't help feeling nervous and scared for him( <i>I have been clinging to my arm rests and was sitting on the edge of my chair while reading this </i> ) because I couldn't imagine how he could get himself out of this absolute trouble he got into.<br /><br />But then,again,I loved how the author crafted a remarkable ending in this trilogy!       <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer873011918" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6205374586878443958">Dear Universe,<br/>I have just finished reading The Shadow Throne, so you may not want to talk to me for a while. And unless you want to hear me jabbering about the sheer awesomeness of Jaron, Mott, and Amarinda, I don't want to talk to you either. You see, this book delivers. Remember in the first book of the trilogy, when Jaron fooled us all with his unreliable narrator skills? Remember the second book, when we bashed our heads into the pages shouting, "What are you doing, you stupid boy? You'll ge</span>
  <span id="freeText6205374586878443958" style="display:none">Dear Universe,<br />I have just finished reading The Shadow Throne, so you may not want to talk to me for a while. And unless you want to hear me jabbering about the sheer awesomeness of Jaron, Mott, and Amarinda, I don't want to talk to you either. You see, this book delivers. Remember in the first book of the trilogy, when Jaron fooled us all with his unreliable narrator skills? Remember the second book, when we bashed our heads into the pages shouting, "What are you doing, you stupid boy? You'll get yourself killed!" Well, the third book is that on steroids. Remember how Imogen was always there to support him, whether that meant cleaning his wounds or hiding kitchen knives so he'd always have access to a weapon? She'll make you cry now. Remember clumsy but brainy Tobias? Remember proud and loyal Amarinda? Guess who ends up together.<br />Remember the pirates? Yeah, this book has more pirates. My only disappointment was that they stayed on dry land the entire time. I would've liked to see them at sea. <br />Jaron is back, and he's the same snarky, savvy boy you grew to love. Even when his life gets put through the wringer, even when everyone he loves is ripped away from him, even when there's no hope for the future-he's always got a plan. You may think you know what happens next but he'll prove you wrong.<br />The ending is action packed and heartwarming all at once. Now, if you'll excuse me, I need to go read over my favorite parts. Goodbye, Internet!<br />Sincerely,<br />Erica</span>
  <a data-text-id="6205374586878443958" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">masochists</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6575298-tessa?shelf=predictable">predictable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6575298-tessa?shelf=the-premise-is-dead">the-premise-is-dead</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer765760130" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8443056946110790439">*headdesk*<br/><br/>I loved the first book. I liked the second. <br/><br/>This one made me want to scream loudly and publicly and then spear it to the wall with my knitting needles. <br/><br/>Nielson's writing wasn't up to par. The entire book consisted of telling versus showing and I was just bored. Look at my read dates. It took me a month to read it because I was reading a copy at B&N and I didn't care enough to go back sooner. I also live an hour away from B&N, but if I was really desperate I could have wrangled it.<br/><br/>I was</span>
  <span id="freeText8443056946110790439" style="display:none">*headdesk*<br /><br />I loved the first book. I liked the second. <br /><br />This one made me want to scream loudly and publicly and then spear it to the wall with my knitting needles. <br /><br />Nielson's writing wasn't up to par. The entire book consisted of telling versus showing and I was just bored. Look at my read dates. It took me a month to read it because I was reading a copy at B&amp;N and I didn't care enough to go back sooner. I also live an hour away from B&amp;N, but if I was really desperate I could have wrangled it.<br /><br />I wasn't really desperate. I didn't care. The book is one pointless, meaningless battle after another with stupid junior high pep talks interspersed (always on horseback as they race from place to place) throughout. The sap and mushiness in this book killed me. <br /><br />Jaron's ideas would never hold weight in the real world. They weren't believable and they depended way too much on outside influences. Every good con artist knows that if you aren't doing it yourself, you shouldn't depend on it. <br /><br />***The next paragraph has vague spoilers***<br /><br /><br />But by far the worst thing was an-event-that-shall-remain-unnamed. It happens early in the book, like the third or fourth chapter. I was shocked and stunned and so impressed that Jennifer Nielson would take such a risk that would anger so many people. Well. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[She didn't. It was a cop-out because Imogen was conveniently saved by unnamed 'herbs' and then the princess fell in love with Tobias so that Jaron could marry her. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> If she had stuck to her guns, the magnificence of what she had done might have redeemed this book for me. The other problems are still glaring, but that would have been a turning point for this book and me. As it played out, though, it was a turning point in the wrong direction. <br /><br />I was so angry when I finished this book. I wish I hadn't read it. If I could take it back, I would. I consider it a complete waste of my time. <br /><br />Okay then. I'm so angry my hands are trembling. I think it's time this stops.</span>

<div id="review_1378804868" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1378804868" />
    <a title="Gavin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin"><img alt="Gavin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338207884p2/8192509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1378804868?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gavin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gavin" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin">Gavin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8192509-gavin?shelf=ya-books">ya-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1378804868" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11130987896357221244">I enjoyed the first two books in <i>The Ascendance Trilogy </i>, but I did not enjoy this final instalment of the series quite as much. <br/><br/>Jaron is now King of Carthya, but he must learn how to lead quickly as Carthya is being invaded by three separate neighbouring countries. The most difficult of the invaders, Avenia, are lead by the vengeful and greedy King Vargan. To complicate matters even further King Vargan has kidnapped Imogen, the girl who Jaron loves. Jaron, with the help of his friends and allie</span>
  <span id="freeText11130987896357221244" style="display:none">I enjoyed the first two books in <i>The Ascendance Trilogy </i>, but I did not enjoy this final instalment of the series quite as much. <br /><br />Jaron is now King of Carthya, but he must learn how to lead quickly as Carthya is being invaded by three separate neighbouring countries. The most difficult of the invaders, Avenia, are lead by the vengeful and greedy King Vargan. To complicate matters even further King Vargan has kidnapped Imogen, the girl who Jaron loves. Jaron, with the help of his friends and allies, must find a way to repel the invasion and rescue Imogen. <br /><br />The story was OK, but nothing special. I found that I was never overly excited by any of the happenings. Though I suspect that could be because they all had a very familiar feel. There is only so many times Jaron and his friends can get captured by their enemies and then escape before it starts to get tiresome! The other big issue I had was that the war story arc was a bit dull. I preferred the parts of the story that focused on the witty banter between the characters and some of the other light adventure sub-plots. <br /><br />I was happy with the way things wrapped up for Jaron and the host of secondary characters that we have grown familiar with over the course of the series. <br /><br />Although this final book was a bit dull I'll remember this children's fantasy series fondly. <br /><br />Rating: 2.5 stars. <br /><br />Audio Note: Charlie McWade was not at his best in this one. I thought he was overdoing things at times. Though I'm not sure if that is his fault or if that is just the way things were written! </span>
  <a data-text-id="11130987896357221244" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9365655516367534045">Not sure what all else I can say about this book. But like any good high fantasy finally, it ends making you feel all warm and fuzzy inside. I love this series, perhaps because of Jaron, who is literally one of my favorite characters that any one has written. And I love his plots and schemes, I love that he always has a plan yet never has a plan. I love a lot of the other characters. Sometimes I wish there was more detail in some of the descriptions (like about Connor) and plots, but over all I </span>
  <span id="freeText9365655516367534045" style="display:none">Not sure what all else I can say about this book. But like any good high fantasy finally, it ends making you feel all warm and fuzzy inside. I love this series, perhaps because of Jaron, who is literally one of my favorite characters that any one has written. And I love his plots and schemes, I love that he always has a plan yet never has a plan. I love a lot of the other characters. Sometimes I wish there was more detail in some of the descriptions (like about Connor) and plots, but over all I think the brevity is also one of it's strong points. All and all a good ending for this series but I'm not sure it was as great as the other two. </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1381205382" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11791093666927348704"><br/>Ugh. My reaction to finishing a book should not be, "Oh, thank goodness that's over!" <br/><br/>This is possibly a three-star book on its own merits, but compared to the first two books in this trilogy, it was a real disappointment. As this aimed for a darker and more serious, mature story line to wrap up Sage's character development from trouble-making boy orphan to a capable, adult king, it lost most of the humor, charm, and cleverness that were such highlights of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12432220.The_False_Prince__The_Ascendance_Trilogy___1_' title='The False Prince (The Ascendance Trilogy, #1) by Jennifer A. Nielsen' rel='nofollow noopener'> The False Prince</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15703770.The_Runaway_King__The_Ascendance_Trilogy___2_' title='The Runaway King (The Ascendance Trilogy, #2) by Jennifer A. Nielsen' rel='nofollow noopener'> The Runaway King</a></span>
  <span id="freeText11791093666927348704" style="display:none"><br />Ugh. My reaction to finishing a book should not be, "Oh, thank goodness that's over!" <br /><br />This is possibly a three-star book on its own merits, but compared to the first two books in this trilogy, it was a real disappointment. As this aimed for a darker and more serious, mature story line to wrap up Sage's character development from trouble-making boy orphan to a capable, adult king, it lost most of the humor, charm, and cleverness that were such highlights of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12432220.The_False_Prince__The_Ascendance_Trilogy___1_" title="The False Prince (The Ascendance Trilogy, #1) by Jennifer A. Nielsen" rel="nofollow noopener"> The False Prince</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15703770.The_Runaway_King__The_Ascendance_Trilogy___2_" title="The Runaway King (The Ascendance Trilogy, #2) by Jennifer A. Nielsen" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Runaway King</a>. His unreliable narrative wore thin for me, and a lot of the material felt recycled rather than surprising. And with the land of Carthya suddenly at war with all its neighbors, the story was a bit grim, which didn't make me eager to keep picking it back up. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Worst of all, the author commits a Cardinal Twist Sin as far as I'm concerned. I thought she'd done something really brave and unexpected, and then it got undone, with no particularly good explanation that I noticed, either. I nearly quit reading right then and there, except there were only about two chapters left at that point. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I still recommend the first two books. But read this one only if you must know every last detail that gets Sage to the fairly predictable happy ending. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11791093666927348704" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14400073184963781130"><b>****4.25 STARS!**** </b><br/><br/>I'm quite <i>shocked</i> honestly. <br/>I really <u>enjoyed</u> reading this novel. <br/>It was <s>kind</s> of dark.<br/>Had a lot of clever plans made by Jaron.<br/>Made me giggle with <i>excitement</i>.<br/>& <i>definitely</i> had my eyes sweaty.<br/>I really <b>like</b> it.<br/><br/><i>

Nielsen" rel="nofollow noopener">Jennifer A. Nielsen</a>. The first book is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12432220.The_False_Prince__The_Ascendance_Trilogy___1_" title="The False Prince (The Ascendance Trilogy, #1) by Jennifer A. Nielsen" rel="nofollow noopener">The False Prince</a>, followed by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15703770.The_Runaway_King__The_Ascendance_Trilogy___2_" title="The Runaway King (The Ascendance Trilogy, #2) by Jennifer A. Nielsen" rel="nofollow noopener">The Runaway King</a>, and lastly <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17667561.The_Shadow_Throne__The_Ascendance_Trilogy___3_" title="The Shadow Throne (The Ascendance Trilogy, #3) by Jennifer A. Nielsen" rel="nofollow noopener">The Shadow Throne</a>. The trilogy started out when Jaron was scouted by Connor to take the role of the lost prince of <i>Carthya</i>. Jaron is just an orphanage boy, and he's far away from being a prince. However, with Connor's help, is he going to succeed?<br><br><a href="http://s1219.photobucket.com/user/meemoo229/media/e6a609f26f67f569d582a5aa5bb787c0.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465568420i/19375018._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo e6a609f26f67f569d582a5aa5bb787c0.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I'm very happy to see how much this trilogy has covered. When I started out reading this, I honestly didn't expect anything, but by the end, I'm very glad I read this. This is a children/Middle Grade trilogy, yet it had some very dark elements. Jaron is definitely too smart to be a fourteen year old boy. The reader got to see character development from so many characters. Imogen, Amarinda, Tobias, Roden, Mott, and even Jaron himself. <br><br><i>
  <blockquote> “One of the greatest kings?” My smile widened. “That’s it? Why not the greatest?”<br><br>“This will only make your arrogance worse, I’m sure.”<br><br>“Really? Do you think that’s possible?” </blockquote>

</a><br><br>The world building of this novel isn't very different from our world, but I still noticed how <i>unique</i> this world was. The writing is <u>rich</u> and<u> clear. </u><br><br>I'm very happy I finished reading this trilogy, and since it's easy to go through, it definitely helped me in getting over my reading slump. <br><br>Recommended to all readers! </span>

<div id="review_970242843" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/970242843" />
    <a title="jv poore" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5157918-jv-poore"><img alt="jv poore" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570108420p2/5157918.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/970242843?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jv poore" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jv poore" href="/user/show/5157918-jv-poore">jv poore</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5157918-jv-poore?shelf=buried-under-books">buried-under-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5157918-jv-poore?shelf=own-it">own-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5157918-jv-poore?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer970242843" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9347563549659594741">Oh how I’ve missed these colorful characters! Jaron’s wit sharpens with anger and whenever he and Roden are in the same country, Jaron fairly idles at anger. Admittedly though, his previous journeys seem to have smoothed out some of his rough edges and forced a bit of maturity. From the first leg of adventure when Jaron, Tobias and Roden were yanked from the orphanage in The False Prince (The Ascendance Trilogy, Book I) , to Jaron’s capture by pirates in The Runaway King (The Ascendance Trilogy,</span>
  <span id="freeText9347563549659594741" style="display:none">Oh how I’ve missed these colorful characters! Jaron’s wit sharpens with anger and whenever he and Roden are in the same country, Jaron fairly idles at anger. Admittedly though, his previous journeys seem to have smoothed out some of his rough edges and forced a bit of maturity. From the first leg of adventure when Jaron, Tobias and Roden were yanked from the orphanage in The False Prince (The Ascendance Trilogy, Book I) , to Jaron’s capture by pirates in The Runaway King (The Ascendance Trilogy, Book II), this young man has had no choice but to learn quickly, fight hard and follow his heart in order to survive.<br /><br />The Shadow Throne (The Ascendance Trilogy, Book III) is quite simply, the quintessential conclusion. Still nursing a broken leg, courtesy of Roden, the young king has no time to focus on healing as his arrival home brings the news that his land of Carthya is targeted for immediate attack from three countries, each coming from a different direction. Compounding the horror, the very girl who captured Jaron’s heart has been taken hostage and is being held by one of the threatening countries. Clearly none of this is a coincidence, but with no time to consider the bigger plan, Jaron rapidly begins barking out orders, only to be reminded that he is no longer alone. Jaron had only recently learned the value of trusted friends. Always open-minded, but now quicker to be flexible, Jaron acknowledges that to conquer, they must divide.<br /> <br />True to nature, first implementations of his new kingly power were unprecedented and shocking. Releasing his betrothed Amarinda from their arranged vows to then declare her a princess of Carthya was unheard of. Knighting the charming chatterbox Fink was ridiculous. The boy couldn’t lift a sword with both hands. <br /><br />When Jaron’s tiny group scattered, his enemy makes the ultimate move. With diabolical focus on the strength of friendship, love and loyalty; Jaron’s nemesis gleefully informs separated individuals immediately whenever a companion has been captured or killed. Details are not spared. Will the youngsters, so strong and cohesive together, find the strength and will to survive solely, in spite of the aching emptiness?<br /><br />Ms. Nielsen impressively combines ferocious battles, brilliantly clever tricks and traps, quick thinking and scintillating dialogue with kindness, empathy and loyalty to end the attack on Carthya. In doing so, many mysteries meandering through the trilogy are resolved without a perceived need to answer each and every question ever raised along the way.<br /><br />To me, Ms. Nielsen has a unique, uncanny ability to reveal more than generally meets the eye, without deliberately and emphatically lecturing. Immersed in her words, I’m wide open. I feel eager to take everything in, mull it over; carefully consider all facets and options. I’m far enough removed to view an entire picture, yet close enough to be totally vested. I’m highly entertained, amused and delighted. Simultaneously, impulsively…I’m reflective. Always, I’m hopeful and happy when visiting the world created by Ms. Nielsen.<br /><br />This review was written for Buried Under Books by jv poore.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9347563549659594741" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_912468230" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/912468230" />
    <a title="haley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20582304-haley"><img alt="haley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546379722p2/20582304.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/912468230?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="haley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="haley" href="/user/show/20582304-haley">haley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20582304-haley?shelf=so-very-disappointing">so-very-disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20582304-haley?shelf=atrocious">atrocious</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20582304-haley?shelf=coulda-been-better">coulda-been-better</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20582304-haley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer912468230" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11826638710600801938">After the first book, the series rapidly went downhill, IMO. I absolutely adored the first book. It was a five-star, gold medal, 1st place brilliant perfection. Second book was a bit of a disappointment, but nonetheless enjoyable.<br/><br/>Then The Shadow Throne happened. And I am so, terribly disappointed in how subpar this is when compared to the brilliance of The False Prince.<br/><br/>Firstly, let's talk about Imogen for a second. Actually, a bit longer than a second, because I have a lot to say about her. I do</span>
  <span id="freeText11826638710600801938" style="display:none">After the first book, the series rapidly went downhill, IMO. I absolutely adored the first book. It was a five-star, gold medal, 1st place brilliant perfection. Second book was a bit of a disappointment, but nonetheless enjoyable.<br /><br />Then The Shadow Throne happened. And I am so, terribly disappointed in how subpar this is when compared to the brilliance of The False Prince.<br /><br />Firstly, let's talk about Imogen for a second. Actually, a bit longer than a second, because I have a lot to say about her. I don't like her. At all. In fact, I hate her. Her mere existence angers me. An editor should have seen that her character serves absolutely no purpose other than to be a bland and boring love interest. She should not be allowed to exist. <br /><br />So, as callous and bitchy as this may sound, I was sort of happy when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Imogen "died". Died is in quotes because SHE DIDN'T ACTUALLY DIE. Why?? You know, I kind of suspected she might be actually alive but I didn't want my suspicions to be right! Why couldn't the author have just left Imogen dead? Her character not only is completely useless, but killing her would have shown that this war is as brutal as it sounds and it would have forced some growth in Jaron/Sage (I still call him Sage because I like that name a whole lot more).  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Speaking of Jaron, I feel like that clever, sarcastic, mischievous boy we all know and love from the first two books was replaced by his evil twin. Jaron's not a mischievous but likable kid in this book, he's just plain stupid. How do his plans even work? They shouldn't but somehow, they do. And I hate how everyone just worships Jaron and follows all his orders without question. Trust me, the kind of shit Jaron pulls off would not fly with me. <br /><br />Okay, another big issue; the ending. Everything is all wrapped up in a neat and tidy package and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Imogen and Jaron get married, Tobias and Amarinda get married, Roden the orphan finds out he actually has a family  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> essentially everyone lives happily ever after and all the kingdoms are at peace! And all that shit happens in one freaking chapter. NO, that is NOT how you end a book. Sure, happy endings are great but I do NOT want everything to suddenly be perfect. <br /><br />One positive thing about The Shadow Throne was that there is a lot of action so it's easy to read and it doesn't drag or anything. <br /><br />So, I decided on two stars. I originally gave this book three stars out of loyalty to the first and second book, but two stars more accurately reflects my feelings. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11826638710600801938" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11841491801619783858" style="display:none">A very satisfying ending to the trilogy, I wish a bit more time was spent at the end of the book instead of a kind of abrupt summation, it felt right. I found this book to be a bit predictable to a certain extent, and I did notice some repetitions in regards to situations the characters find themselves in. I really enjoyed the characters, the plot isn't super deep, but I think the ability for the author to make the reader connect with the characters rectifies that. Anyway overall a great, quick and fun trilogy read. Unfortunately the first of the trilogy was my favourite but none the less the second and third were good in their own regard! </span>

<div id="review_1369919837" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1369919837" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1369919837?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1369919837" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1325031688585735722">The Shadow Throne ends our journey with Jaron and company. It answers the questions will Carthya be saved and who will sit on the throne once and for all. But even though Jaron is as snarky as ever this final books had a little something missing for me. There was a large chunk in the center during the war that I lost interest in and I often wondered how many times Jaron could go rushing into some enemy camp just to be caught and tortured. <br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Avenia thinks they're battling a king. I doubt t</b></i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText1325031688585735722" style="display:none">The Shadow Throne ends our journey with Jaron and company. It answers the questions will Carthya be saved and who will sit on the throne once and for all. But even though Jaron is as snarky as ever this final books had a little something missing for me. There was a large chunk in the center during the war that I lost interest in and I often wondered how many times Jaron could go rushing into some enemy camp just to be caught and tortured. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Avenia thinks they're battling a king. I doubt they're prepared to fight a boy who thinks childish pranks are practical strategies for war."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />For a king of Carthya Jaron spends almost no time in the Palace and he seems to always be tromping off to do the things he is supposed to as king send others to do. It does make for an interesting story to have the King sneaking around in the forest playing with the enemy a little like Robin Hood. I liked the times that Jaron is free and working with his friends to win the war. He actually has some friends now and that is a complicated thing for him.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Villains and plots and enemies are simple things to me. But friendships are complicated, and love is harder still. It has wounded me deeper than a sword ever could.” </i>
</blockquote><br />But there are problems with the book. Specifically the pacing in the middle. It became a bit of a trudge for me as they are in the middle of the war. I lost complete interest in the book. The other problem is how indestructible Jaron became. He is caught and tortured and practically at death's door and then poof he is running, fighting, climbing the cliffs of insanity. It was just too much.<br /><br />I liked the last 10% maybe more than the rest of the book. The wrap up was done pretty nicely. But this was my least favorite of the series.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1325031688585735722" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1996981358" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1996981358" />
    <a title="Justine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18656418-justine"><img alt="Justine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588653801p2/18656418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1996981358?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justine" href="/user/show/18656418-justine">Justine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18656418-justine?shelf=read-with-my-kids">read-with-my-kids</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18656418-justine?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18656418-justine?shelf=2017-read">2017-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1996981358" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer559438498124791313">I thought this was a really good finish to the series. <br/><br/>I listened to this on audio with my kids, and the narration was excellent. Yes, maybe the story does tie up everything a little too neatly, but hey, it's middle grade fantasy, and it does that genre very well. My kids actually clapped as we listened to some of the final scenes, so that right there is worth something.<br/><br/>The series as a whole is very enjoyable, and I loved being able to experience it with my kids.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_827163429" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/827163429" />
    <a title="Jon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4277731-jon"><img alt="Jon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1384212540p2/4277731.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/827163429?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jon" href="/user/show/4277731-jon">Jon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4277731-jon?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer827163429" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11149879360851797748"><a href='http://scottreadsit.blogspot.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Check out Scott Reads It for reviews, giveaways, & more!</a><br/><br/> It's such a bittersweet feeling when you have to say goodbye to one of your favorite series. I only became a fan of The Ascendance Trilogy recently, but I know this is one of those series that will stay with me for years to come. Jennifer A. Nielsen has written one of the best fantasy I've read in years and I really hate to say goodbye to beloved characters like Jaron and Imogen. Though it saddens me thinking that this trilogy is over, I a</span>
  <span id="freeText11149879360851797748" style="display:none"><a href="http://scottreadsit.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Check out Scott Reads It for reviews, giveaways, &amp; more!</a><br /><br /> It's such a bittersweet feeling when you have to say goodbye to one of your favorite series. I only became a fan of The Ascendance Trilogy recently, but I know this is one of those series that will stay with me for years to come. Jennifer A. Nielsen has written one of the best fantasy I've read in years and I really hate to say goodbye to beloved characters like Jaron and Imogen. Though it saddens me thinking that this trilogy is over, I absolutely loved the way the conclusion unfolds and The Shadow Throne ends with such a bang. The Shadow Throne is a worthy end to a series of this caliber and the finale is absolutely perfect.<br /><br /> Oh Jaron, how I will miss you and your shenanigans. Jaron is one of my all-time favorite male protagonists and he's up there with legends like Harry Potter and Percy Jackson. Jaron is so clever and I admire how he always manages to outwit even the sharpest adults. He has an endless surplus of courage and determination and his intense loyalty towards his friends is unbelievably incredible. There became a point in TST where I just couldn't handle how Jaron was taking so many risks and putting his life on the line, but I knew that it someone had to take these risks to save Carthya. <br /><br /> The Shadow Throne is an emotional hurricane and readers will absolutely need a plethora of tissues while reading this book. I had so many feelings surging through me while reading TST and all of them while reading. Readers will need to emotionally prepare themselves for this one because there are just so many heartfelt, powerful moments. Nielsen has really created such vibrant characters that readers absolutely love and seeing them face any sort of conflict is truly painful. <br /><br /> The romance in this series has been pretty light and The Shadow Throne adds a bit more of a romantic angle to the plot. The romance between Imogen and Jaron is simple, sweet, and I just love the way Nielsen handles it. Nielsen doesn't move the plot forward using the romance, nor does she make the romance the focus of the story by any means. This is a series about a kingdom in chaos and the romance is a sweet little treat in the midst all of the kingdom politics. <br /><br /> I really love Jaron and Imogen because they truly complement each other and their relationship is an equal healthy one. Jaron accepts that Imogen is a strong-willed, courageous women and that doesn't distort his feelings for her in any way. Imogen is such a clever heroine and literature needs more tough female characters that kids can look up to. <br /><br /> I absolutely loved The Shadow Throne and it's such a fitting end to a brilliant series. The Ascendance Trilogy is one of my all-time favorite series and I'm so excited to read Nielsen's upcoming The Praetor War. I definitely think you should start The False Prince because if you haven't, you're missing out on a superb series! This series isn't really for those looking for romance, but I know that readers looking to be captivated by action and adventure will fall in love with The Ascendance Trilogy. The Shadow Throne is everything I expected and just so much more, I will definitely be rereading this series in the future because it's just that great. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11149879360851797748" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1305428390" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1305428390" />
    <a title="Lonna | FLYLēF" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42319420-lonna-flyl-f"><img alt="Lonna | FLYLēF" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1431746518p2/42319420.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1305428390?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lonna | FLYLēF" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lonna | FLYLēF" href="/user/show/42319420-lonna-flyl-f">Lonna | FLYLēF</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1305428390" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2724801592887925824"><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1432224148i/14910585.png' alt='FLYLeF Book Reviews' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Original Post: <a href='http://reviews.flylef.com/2015/06/the-shadow-throne.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <em>The Shadow Throne</em>
</a> at <a href='http://www.flylef.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>FLYLeF</a> (<a href='http://www.flylef.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>www.flylef.com</a>)<br/><br/>IT'S ALWAYS QUITE bittersweet to reach the end of a series, particular one that I have enjoyed thoroughly and has tucked me into bed quite soundly in the early hours of the morning. <a href='http://reviews.flylef.com/2015/06/the-shadow-throne.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <em>The Shadow Throne</em>
</a>, by Jennifer Nielson, is the final installment in <em>The Ascendance Trilogy</em>. And, it does NOT disappoint!<br/><br/>Though born into royalty, life has been anything but easy for Jaron. From outwitting Connor Bevin’s treasonous game in <a href='http://reviews.flylef.com/2015/05/the-false-prince.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <em>The False</em></a></span>
  <span id="freeText2724801592887925824" style="display:none"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1432224148i/14910585.png" alt="FLYLeF Book Reviews" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Original Post: <a href="http://reviews.flylef.com/2015/06/the-shadow-throne.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>The Shadow Throne</em>
</a> at <a href="http://www.flylef.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">FLYLeF</a> (<a href="http://www.flylef.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">www.flylef.com</a>)<br><br>IT'S ALWAYS QUITE bittersweet to reach the end of a series, particular one that I have enjoyed thoroughly and has tucked me into bed quite soundly in the early hours of the morning. <a href="http://reviews.flylef.com/2015/06/the-shadow-throne.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>The Shadow Throne</em>
</a>, by Jennifer Nielson, is the final installment in <em>The Ascendance Trilogy</em>. And, it does NOT disappoint!<br><br>Though born into royalty, life has been anything but easy for Jaron. From outwitting Connor Bevin’s treasonous game in <a href="http://reviews.flylef.com/2015/05/the-false-prince.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>The False Prince</em>
</a>, to conquering the Avenia Pirates in <a href="http://reviews.flylef.com/2015/05/the-runaway-king.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>The Runaway King</em>
</a>, Jaron returns in <a href="http://reviews.flylef.com/2015/06/the-shadow-throne.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>The Shadow Throne</em>
</a> as the Ascendance King of Carthya.<br><br>But…War is here.<br><br>And, it’s here with a vengeance! Three countries launch simultaneous attacks on Carthya with King Vargan of Avenia stopping at nothing until Jaron meets his demise, including the kidnapping of Imogen. Conflicted, Jaron must choose between his kingdom or his heart.<br><br>Everything that could go wrong…does. Imogen is imprisoned, the Princess Amarinda is missing, Roden and Tobias are flung far and wide across Carthya. In a desperate attempt to save his country and the people he loves, Jaron embarks on a daring, if reckless, attempt to change the course of the war. Despite the terrible disadvantages that Jaron constantly faces, there is always an undercurrent of something more than Jaron lets readers on. And as the outcome of the war changes its trajectory many-folds, reads will be left guessing until the very end who will be victorious.<br><br>By far, this Jaron has been quite enjoyable to read. The lost of those dear to him, the positive people he surrounds himself with, and the responsibilities that he shoulders as king, have groomed him into a remarkable young man full of compassion and some humility. Though, readers will still enjoy his lightening-quick wit. I found myself passing the time in my son’s martial arts class, giggling like an idiot, to Jaron’s remarks punctuated precisely at the right moment in the storyline to deliver the perfect punch line.<br><br>It is a difficult thing – to write an ending that appeals to everyone. The last few chapters felt rushed, with a highly unexpected twist that came out of nowhere with a particular foe. Regardless, Ms. Nielson writes with such fervor and excitement that she has a fan in me. Until your next book Ms. Nielson…</span>

<div id="review_2706578330" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2706578330" />
    <a title="Sarah Grace Grzy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59507807-sarah-grace-grzy"><img alt="Sarah Grace Grzy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570047933p2/59507807.jpg" /></a>

  <span id="freeText15900521938751411501" style="display:none">(2.5 stars) Decent book, good series. All in all a typical book/series. It was like a kiddy version of Game of Thrones but only from Jaron's perspective instead of multi-dimensional character perspectives.<br /><br />Lots happened in this final installment of the Ascendance Trilogy. It was too rushed and jumpy. I prefer a book that takes it slow and is more descriptive. It felt more like 'he went there, then came here, and they did this, and then this happened' - instead of describing all the elements and dimensions of it. It felt like Nielsen just wanted to get the story over and done with lol <br /><br />The story was pretty decent but I had issues with the characters:<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />- Jaron - I enjoy his humor, wittiness, and smart-assness about him. But he had way too much responsibility for a kid lol and seemed wayyyyy too mature for his age, buy hey this is a middle school book<br />- Connor is literally the most bouncy loyalty character I have ever read about lol<br />- Mott was such a clingy, needy, undying servant, and felt unrealistic because it happened too quickly and easily in the first couple books<br />- Imogen - I still don't know or understand why Jaron loved her so much, there wasn't enough development through the books to believe it. I knew that in this book the enemy would take her or kill her. And when they said they killed her I knew they must have not killed her because that would be so dumb killing off a valuable hostage to Jaron, it wouldn't make any sense. So the twist that she was actually alive was pretty lame. Also the fact that the enemy asked Jaron about what he wanted on her gravestone was dumb too, why would an enemy do that when he's being all threatening lol.<br />- Ronan - his growth as a leader felt way too quickly earned<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7185147334856633830">I have one student who's already waiting to get their hands on this book, which is why I finished it so fast. Of all the books in this series, this one is probably the most realistic.I will admit to flipping to the end pretty early, to discover that the series ended pretty much exactly as I predicted it would, but the journey from the beginning to that predicted ending was far more satisfying than it has been in past books. There aren't any flagrant moments of deus ex rescue, although there are </span>
  <span id="freeText7185147334856633830" style="display:none">I have one student who's already waiting to get their hands on this book, which is why I finished it so fast. Of all the books in this series, this one is probably the most realistic.I will admit to flipping to the end pretty early, to discover that the series ended pretty much exactly as I predicted it would, but the journey from the beginning to that predicted ending was far more satisfying than it has been in past books. There aren't any flagrant moments of deus ex rescue, although there are moments of "Why did you hide this important detail?," and all of the characters behave as they've been built to behave over the course of the series. Not revolutionary, but pleasant, and all wrapped up in the end, which is especially nice.<br /><br />When I walked out of the bedroom to get another book, I turned to my husband and said, "Books like this are what make me happy for civilian control of the military," and then we had a good discussion of just how ridiculous it is to be able to lose your military and political leader all in one cataclysmic battle (complete with analysis of the Roman dual-consul system--we're nerdy like that). Also, boys should probably not be kings, but if they must, Jaron turned out not to be a bad candidate.</span>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1163228-colleen-houck?shelf=death">death</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1163228-colleen-houck?shelf=risk-taking">risk-taking</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1163228-colleen-houck?shelf=war">war</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1163228-colleen-houck?shelf=military">military</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1163228-colleen-houck?shelf=secrets">secrets</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1914283953" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13869644339959003520">A satisfying conclusion to the series. There were a lot of times I was concerned for the boy king's life and wondered how he was going to get himself out of the situations he put himself in, but that kept me reading. All the characters came together in the end and it was cool to see how their lives all worked out. Love Jaron's sarcasm.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/898162727?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren Stoolfire" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren Stoolfire" href="/user/show/6857324-lauren-stoolfire">Lauren Stoolfire</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/27396631-the-shadow-throne">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6857324-lauren-stoolfire?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6857324-lauren-stoolfire?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6857324-lauren-stoolfire?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6857324-lauren-stoolfire?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6857324-lauren-stoolfire?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer898162727" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16373290422941492936">War has reached Carthya and Jaron has learned that King Vargan of Avenia has kidnapped Imogen in order to bring Jaron's kingdom to it's knees. Jaron knows that he has to make the dangerous rescue attempt in order to save everything he loves - Imogen and his country. As war descends around him, everything that can go wrong does. In the end, these questions remain: Who will survive and who will reign once the war finally ends?<br/><br/><i>The Shadow Throne</i> is a fantastic conclusion to <i>The Ascendance Trilogy</i>. I</span>
  <span id="freeText16373290422941492936" style="display:none">War has reached Carthya and Jaron has learned that King Vargan of Avenia has kidnapped Imogen in order to bring Jaron's kingdom to it's knees. Jaron knows that he has to make the dangerous rescue attempt in order to save everything he loves - Imogen and his country. As war descends around him, everything that can go wrong does. In the end, these questions remain: Who will survive and who will reign once the war finally ends?<br /><br /><i>The Shadow Throne</i> is a fantastic conclusion to <i>The Ascendance Trilogy</i>. I'm sad to have reached the end of the series, but I'm so glad to have had the chance to follow Jaron's journey and meet so many fantastic characters that will stick in my memory. This final installment wraps everything up well and successfully includes all of the elements that made me love the series in the first place. I'm looking forward to reading more of Jennifer A. Nielsen's brilliant work, specifically <i>Mark of the Thief</i>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16373290422941492936" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Vy97ueLTJawMN8oeM6Jnmd7WgPG7Zm/qKhe4lPnnxs2SJQ4YZj44chsE+XwzIPhs4I2eSI6q2/YydbDT8RsjNA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('XPDbrPf7pNYi2knHKcDOF6mkzRigZ95Z80DoJr/v07OZ+q4Ncxa5CDXpeqUpQlHil//ToZWrakXrIuBhtxM2Sg==')})
  }
//]]>
